[Configuration-Driven Behaviors](#11-configuration-driven-behaviors)\n12. [Common Patterns and Best Practices](#12-common-patterns-and-best-practices)\n\n---\n\n## 1. Overview and Threading Model\n\n`KafkaConsumer` is a client that consumes records from a Kafka cluster. It transparently handles broker failures and partition migrations, and coordinates group-based load balancing when a `group.id` is configured.\n\n### Threading Model\n\n**The consumer is NOT thread-safe.** All API calls must be made from the same thread. Concurrent access from multiple threads results in `ConcurrentModificationException`.\n\n**The single exception is `wakeup()`**, which is explicitly designed to be called from an external thread to interrupt a blocking `poll()`, `commitSync()`, or other blocking operation. The interrupted thread receives a `WakeupException`.\n\n```java\n// Thread-safe shutdown pattern\npublic class KafkaConsumerRunner implements Runnable {\n    private final AtomicBoolean closed = new AtomicBoolean(false);\n    private final KafkaConsumer<String, String> consumer;\n\n    public KafkaConsumerRunner(KafkaConsumer<String, String> consumer) {\n        this.consumer = consumer;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void run() {\n        try {\n            consumer.subscribe(Arrays.asList(\"my-topic\"));\n            while (!closed.get()) {\n                ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(10_000));\n                // process records\n            }\n        } catch (WakeupException e) {\n            // Ignore if we are shutting down\n            if (!closed.get()) throw e;\n        } finally {\n            consumer.close();\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Called from any thread\n    public void shutdown() {\n        closed.set(true);\n        consumer.wakeup();\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### Event Loop Model\n\nThe consumer operates on an event loop driven by `poll()`. Group membership heartbeats, rebalance protocol messages, async commit callbacks, and `ConsumerRebalanceListener` callbacks all execute **within** the `poll()` call on the consumer thread. Nothing happens in the background outside of `poll()`.\n\n### Group Membership\n\nWhen `group.id` is set and `subscribe()` is used, the consumer participates in group coordination:\n- Joins the group automatically on the first `poll()` call.\n- Sends periodic heartbeats to the broker.\n- Participates in rebalances when group membership or topic metadata changes.\n- Proactively leaves the group if `max.poll.interval.ms` is exceeded.\n\nWhen `assign()` is used instead, all group coordination is disabled. The consumer acts independently even if it shares a `group.id` with other consumers.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Core Types\n\n### `KafkaConsumer<K, V>`\n\nThe main consumer class. Parameterized by the key type `K` and value type `V` of consumed records.\n\n### `ConsumerRecord<K, V>`\n\nRepresents a single record received from Kafka. Fields:\n\n| Field | Type | Description |\n|-------|------|-------------|\n| `topic()` | `String` | Topic the record came from |\n| `partition()` | `int` | Partition within the topic |\n| `offset()` | `long` | Offset within the partition |\n| `timestamp()` | `long` | Producer-assigned timestamp (ms since epoch), or `NO_TIMESTAMP` |\n| `timestampType()` | `TimestampType` | `CREATE_TIME`, `LOG_APPEND_TIME`, or `NO_TIMESTAMP_TYPE` |\n| `key()` | `K` | Deserialized key (may be `null`) |\n| `value()` | `V` | Deserialized value |\n| `headers()` | `Headers` | Mutable collection of record headers |\n| `leaderEpoch()` | `Optional<Integer>` | Leader epoch at time of write; used in offset commits |\n| `serializedKeySize()` | `int` | Byte size of the serialized key, or `-1` |\n| `serializedValueSize()` | `int` | Byte size of the serialized value, or `-1` |\n\n> **Thread safety:** `ConsumerRecord` is **not thread-safe**. The `headers()` collection is mutable and must not be accessed concurrently. Individual `Header` instances are read-safe but must not be modified concurrently.\n\n### `ConsumerRecords<K, V>`\n\nContainer returned by `poll()`, holding records grouped by `TopicPartition`.\n\n| Method | Description |\n|--------|-------------|\n| `records(TopicPartition)` | List of records for a specific partition |\n| `records(String topic)` | Iterable over all records for a topic |\n| `partitions()` | Set of `TopicPartition` values with records |\n| `nextOffsets()` | Map of `TopicPartition` → `OffsetAndMetadata` for the next offset to commit (available since 4.0) |\n| `iterator()` | Iterates all records across all partitions |\n| `isEmpty()` | Returns `true` if no records were returned |\n| `count()` | Total number of records across all partitions |\n\n`ConsumerRecords.EMPTY` is a singleton empty result set.\n\n### `ConsumerRebalanceListener`\n\nCallback interface invoked during partition rebalances. See [Section 12.3](#123-rebalance-listener-with-manual-offset-management) for usage.\n\n### `OffsetAndMetadata`\n\nCarries an offset value, an optional `leaderEpoch`, and optional string metadata. Used in commit calls and `committed()` queries.\n\n### `OffsetAndTimestamp`\n\nReturn type of `offsetsForTimes()`. Contains the matched offset and the corresponding timestamp.\n\n### `TopicPartition`\n\nImmutable value object identifying a specific partition: `(topic: String, partition: int)`.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Constructor Variants and Configuration\n\nAll constructors ultimately create an internal `ConsumerDelegate` via `ConsumerDelegateCreator`. After construction, always call `close()` to avoid TCP connection leaks.\n\n### `KafkaConsumer(Map<String, Object> configs)`\n\n```java\nKafkaConsumer(Map<String, Object> configs)\n```\n\nCreates a consumer from a configuration map. Deserializers must be specified via `key.deserializer` and `value.deserializer` config keys.\n\n### `KafkaConsumer(Properties properties)`\n\n```java\nKafkaConsumer(Properties properties)\n```\n\nCreates a consumer from a `Properties` object. Equivalent to the map-based constructor.\n\n### `KafkaConsumer(Properties properties, Deserializer<K> keyDeserializer, Deserializer<V> valueDeserializer)`\n\n```java\nKafkaConsumer(Properties properties,\n              Deserializer<K> keyDeserializer,\n              Deserializer<V> valueDeserializer)\n```\n\nPasses deserializers directly. When deserializers are provided this way, their `configure()` method is **not** called by the consumer — the caller is responsible for any initialization.\n\n### `KafkaConsumer(Map<String, Object> configs, Deserializer<K> keyDeserializer, Deserializer<V> valueDeserializer)`\n\n```java\nKafkaConsumer(Map<String, Object> configs,\n              Deserializer<K> keyDeserializer,\n              Deserializer<V> valueDeserializer)\n```\n\nMap-based variant that also accepts pre-configured deserializers.\n\n### Minimum Required Configuration\n\n| Property | Description |\n|----------|-------------|\n| `bootstrap.servers` | Comma-separated `host:port` pairs for initial cluster contact |\n| `key.deserializer` | Fully-qualified class name of the key `Deserializer` |\n| `value.deserializer` | Fully-qualified class name of the value `Deserializer` |\n\nFor group-managed consumption, `group.id` is also required.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Subscription and Assignment Methods\n\nSubscription (dynamic group assignment) and manual assignment are **mutually exclusive**. Calling `subscribe()` after `assign()` (without an intervening `unsubscribe()`) throws `IllegalStateException`, and vice versa.\n\n### 4.1 Dynamic Subscription (Group Management)\n\n#### `subscribe(Collection<String> topics, ConsumerRebalanceListener listener)`\n\n```java\nvoid subscribe(Collection<String> topics, ConsumerRebalanceListener listener)\n```\n\nSubscribes to the specified topics. Kafka automatically assigns partitions among group members. Topic subscriptions are **not incremental** — this call replaces any prior subscription.\n\n- Passing an empty collection is equivalent to calling `unsubscribe()`.\n- Rebalances are triggered when the group membership changes or partition counts change.\n- The listener is invoked during `poll()` when partitions are revoked or assigned.\n- **Throws:** `IllegalArgumentException` if `topics` or `listener` is null, or topics contain null/empty elements. `IllegalStateException` if `assign()` was previously called, or if no partition assignment strategy is configured.\n\n#### `subscribe(Collection<String> topics)`\n\n```java\nvoid subscribe(Collection<String> topics)\n```\n\nShorthand for `subscribe(topics, noOpListener)`. If you need to commit offsets before a rebalance completes, use the overload with a `ConsumerRebalanceListener`.\n\n#### `subscribe(Pattern pattern, ConsumerRebalanceListener listener)`\n\n```java\nvoid subscribe(Pattern pattern, ConsumerRebalanceListener listener)\n```\n\nSubscribes to all topics matching a `java.util.regex.Pattern`. Pattern matching runs periodically against all existing topics (controlled by `metadata.max.age.ms`). Newly created topics matching the pattern are automatically picked up.\n\n#### `subscribe(Pattern pattern)`\n\n```java\nvoid subscribe(Pattern pattern)\n```\n\nNo-op listener variant of the pattern subscription.\n\n#### `subscribe(SubscriptionPattern pattern, ConsumerRebalanceListener listener)`\n\n```java\nvoid subscribe(SubscriptionPattern pattern, ConsumerRebalanceListener listener)\n```\n\n**CONSUMER group protocol only.** Subscribes using a Google RE2/J-compatible regular expression, enabling server-side topic matching. If the pattern is not RE2/J-compatible, an `InvalidRegularExpression` is thrown on the next `poll()`.\n\n#### `subscribe(SubscriptionPattern pattern)`\n\n```java\nvoid subscribe(SubscriptionPattern pattern)\n```\n\nNo-op listener variant of the RE2/J pattern subscription.\n\n### 4.2 Manual Assignment\n\n#### `assign(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions)`\n\n```java\nvoid assign(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions)\n```\n\nManually assigns specific `TopicPartition`s to this consumer. Disables all group coordination — no rebalances, no heartbeats for group purposes. Passing an empty collection is equivalent to `unsubscribe()`.\n\n- If auto-commit is enabled, an async commit of the old assignment is triggered before the new assignment takes effect.\n- Each consumer acts independently even if it shares a `group.id` with others. To avoid offset commit conflicts, use a unique `group.id` per consumer instance.\n- **Throws:** `IllegalArgumentException` if `partitions` is null or contains null/empty topics. `IllegalStateException` if `subscribe()` was previously called.\n\n### 4.3 Unsubscribing\n\n#### `unsubscribe()`\n\n```java\nvoid unsubscribe()\n```\n\nClears all subscriptions (topic list, pattern, or RE2/J pattern) and also clears any manually assigned partitions. This allows switching between subscription and assignment modes.\n\n- **Throws:** `KafkaException` for rebalance callback errors.\n\n### 4.4 Querying Subscription State\n\n#### `subscription()`\n\n```java\nSet<String> subscription()\n```\n\nReturns the set of topics from the most recent `subscribe(Collection, ...)` call. Returns an empty set if no topic subscription has been made.\n\n#### `assignment()`\n\n```java\nSet<TopicPartition> assignment()\n```\n\nReturns the set of `TopicPartition`s currently assigned. For manually assigned consumers, returns exactly what was passed to `assign()`. For subscribed consumers, returns the current auto-assigned partitions (may be empty if assignment has not yet been established or is in progress).\n\n---\n\n## 5. Polling and Data Fetching\n\n### `poll(Duration timeout)`\n\n```java\nConsumerRecords<K, V> poll(Duration timeout)\n```\n\nThe primary method for fetching records. It also drives all background activity: group coordination, heartbeats, async commit callbacks, and rebalance listener invocations.\n\n**Return behavior:**\n- Returns immediately if records are already available in the fetch buffer.\n- Returns immediately if the position advances past control records or aborted transactions (when `isolation.level=read_committed`).\n- Otherwise blocks up to `timeout`. Returns an empty `ConsumerRecords` if no records arrive within that window.\n\n**Important behavioral notes:**\n\n1. **Timeout is not a hard bound.** `poll()` may block *longer* than the specified timeout to execute `ConsumerRebalanceListener` callbacks. Plan for this when setting timeouts.\n\n2. **Rebalances occur only during `poll()`.** Group coordination messages (join group, sync group, heartbeats) are processed only within the `poll()` call. If you stop calling `poll()`, the group stalls.\n\n3. **`max.poll.interval.ms` enforcement.** If `poll()` is not called within the configured interval, the consumer proactively sends a LeaveGroup request and is removed from the group. This triggers a `CommitFailedException` if a `commitSync()` is subsequently attempted.\n\n4. **`IllegalStateException` if not subscribed.** Calling `poll()` without a prior `subscribe()` or `assign()` throws immediately.\n\n5. **Auto-subscription join.** For subscribed consumers, the first `poll()` triggers the JoinGroup exchange with the coordinator and establishes the initial assignment.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `timeout` — Maximum time to block. Must be `>= 0` and `<= Long.MAX_VALUE` milliseconds.\n\n**Throws:**\n\n| Exception | Condition |\n|-----------|-----------|\n| `WakeupException` | `wakeup()` was called before or during this call |\n| `InterruptException` | The calling thread was interrupted |\n| `InvalidOffsetException` | Offset for a partition is undefined or out of range and no reset policy is configured |\n| `AuthenticationException` | Authentication with the broker failed |\n| `AuthorizationException` | Consumer lacks `Read` access to subscribed topics or the configured `group.id` |\n| `InvalidTopicException` | A subscribed topic name is invalid |\n| `FencedInstanceIdException` | This consumer instance was fenced by the broker |\n| `UnsupportedVersionException` | Broker does not support stable offsets (with `read_committed`) or RE2/J subscriptions |\n| `KafkaException` | Any other unrecoverable error (invalid group ID, session timeout, deserialization failure, rebalance callback exception) |\n| `IllegalArgumentException` | `timeout` is negative |\n| `IllegalStateException` | Consumer is not subscribed or assigned to any partitions |\n| `ArithmeticException` | `timeout` exceeds `Long.MAX_VALUE` milliseconds |\n\n---\n\n## 6. Offset Management\n\n### 6.1 Understanding Offset Concepts\n\nKafka tracks consumer position using several related concepts:\n\n| Concept | Definition |\n|---------|------------|\n| **Position** | The offset of the *next* record that `poll()` will return. One greater than the highest offset seen so far in that partition. Advances automatically on each `poll()`. |\n| **Committed offset** | The offset durably stored in Kafka (or your external store). On restart or rebalance, the consumer resumes from this offset. **Must be the offset of the next record to process**, not the last consumed record. |\n| **Beginning offset** | The earliest available offset in the partition (log start offset). May be > 0 on compacted or retention-bounded topics. |\n| **End offset (HWM)** | High watermark — offset of the last successfully replicated message plus one (`read_uncommitted`). |\n| **Last Stable Offset (LSO)** | Minimum of HWM and the smallest offset of any open transaction. The effective end for `read_committed` consumers. |\n\n**Key rule:** When committing, always commit `nextRecord.offset()` (the record you want to read *next*), not the offset of the last record you processed. Use `ConsumerRecords.nextOffsets()` for a convenient per-partition map.\n\n```java\n// CORRECT: commit the offset of the NEXT record to process\nlong nextOffset = lastRecord.offset() + 1;\nconsumer.commitSync(Map.of(partition, new OffsetAndMetadata(nextOffset)));\n\n// Or using ConsumerRecords.nextOffsets() (preferred since Kafka 4.0)\nconsumer.commitSync(records.nextOffsets());\n```\n\n### 6.2 Synchronous Commit\n\n#### `commitSync()`\n\n```java\nvoid commitSync()\n```\n\nCommits the offsets of all records returned by the most recent `poll()`. Blocks until the commit succeeds, an unrecoverable error is thrown, or `default.api.timeout.ms` expires (`TimeoutException`).\n\nAny pending async commits are guaranteed to have their callbacks invoked before this method returns (consumer group protocol only).\n\n#### `commitSync(Duration timeout)`\n\n```java\nvoid commitSync(Duration timeout)\n```\n\nSame as `commitSync()` but with an explicit timeout instead of the default.\n\n#### `commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> offsets)`\n\n```java\nvoid commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> offsets)\n```\n\nCommits the specified offsets for the specified partitions. The map is copied internally — safe to mutate after the call. When using group management, committed offsets must belong to currently assigned partitions.\n\nInclude the `leaderEpoch` from `ConsumerRecord.leaderEpoch()` or `ConsumerRecords.nextOffsets()` for epoch-aware fencing.\n\n#### `commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> offsets, Duration timeout)`\n\n```java\nvoid commitSync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> offsets, Duration timeout)\n```\n\nExplicit offsets with an explicit timeout.\n\n**Throws for all `commitSync` variants:**\n\n| Exception | Condition |\n|-----------|-----------|\n| `CommitFailedException` | Commit failed with a non-retriable error (typically group rebalanced away before commit) |\n| `RebalanceInProgressException` | Consumer is mid-rebalance; call `poll()` to complete the rebalance then retry |\n| `TimeoutException` | Commit did not complete within the timeout |\n| `WakeupException` | `wakeup()` called before or during |\n| `InterruptException` | Thread was interrupted |\n| `AuthenticationException` / `AuthorizationException` | Security failures |\n| `FencedInstanceIdException` | Instance fenced (classic group protocol) |\n| `KafkaException` | Other unrecoverable errors |\n\n### 6.3 Asynchronous Commit\n\n#### `commitAsync()`\n\n```java\nvoid commitAsync()\n```\n\nEquivalent to `commitAsync(null)`. Commits last-polled offsets without blocking.\n\n#### `commitAsync(OffsetCommitCallback callback)`\n\n```java\nvoid commitAsync(OffsetCommitCallback callback)\n```\n\nCommits last-polled offsets asynchronously. The `callback` receives the committed offsets (or an exception) when the commit completes. Callbacks are invoked during the next `poll()` call.\n\n#### `commitAsync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> offsets, OffsetCommitCallback callback)`\n\n```java\nvoid commitAsync(Map<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> offsets, OffsetCommitCallback callback)\n```\n\nCommits specific offsets asynchronously.\n\n**Async commit behavior notes:**\n\n- **No internal retry.** Unlike `commitSync()`, `commitAsync()` does **not** retry on failure. A failed async commit is simply passed to the callback (if provided) or silently discarded. This is intentional: retrying an outdated offset after a successful later commit would regress the committed position.\n- **Ordering guarantee.** Multiple `commitAsync()` calls are sent in invocation order. Callbacks are also invoked in order.\n- **Flushes before sync.** A subsequent `commitSync()` is guaranteed to complete only after all prior `commitAsync()` callbacks have fired.\n- **`FencedInstanceIdException`** may be thrown immediately if the instance is fenced.\n\n### 6.4 Seeking (Position Control)\n\n#### `seek(TopicPartition partition, long offset)`\n\n```java\nvoid seek(TopicPartition partition, long offset)\n```\n\nOverrides the fetch offset for the given partition. The next `poll()` will return records starting at `offset` (if such a record exists). The seek takes effect on the **next** fetch request; the consumer may wait up to `fetch.max.wait.ms` before fetching from the new position.\n\nIf the offset is below the log start offset or above the log end offset, the behavior is controlled by `auto.offset.reset`:\n- `earliest` — seeks to the beginning\n- `latest` — seeks to the end\n- `none` — throws `OffsetOutOfRangeException`\n\n**Throws:** `IllegalArgumentException` if offset is negative. `IllegalStateException` if the partition is not assigned.\n\n#### `seek(TopicPartition partition, OffsetAndMetadata offsetAndMetadata)`\n\n```java\nvoid seek(TopicPartition partition, OffsetAndMetadata offsetAndMetadata)\n```\n\nSame as the long-offset variant but also sets the leader epoch for epoch-aware fencing.\n\n#### `seekToBeginning(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions)`\n\n```java\nvoid seekToBeginning(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions)\n```\n\nSeeks to the first available (earliest) offset of each given partition. **Evaluates lazily** — the actual position is only resolved on the next `poll()` or `position()` call. If `partitions` is empty, seeks all currently assigned partitions.\n\n**Throws:** `IllegalArgumentException` if `partitions` is null. `IllegalStateException` if any partition is not assigned.\n\n#### `seekToEnd(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions)`\n\n```java\nvoid seekToEnd(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions)\n```\n\nSeeks to the last offset of each partition. **Evaluates lazily**. For `read_committed` consumers, the effective end is the LSO, not the HWM.\n\n**Throws:** `IllegalArgumentException` if `partitions` is null. `IllegalStateException` if any partition is not assigned.\n\n### 6.5 Querying Committed Offsets\n\n#### `committed(Set<TopicPartition> partitions)`\n\n```java\nMap<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> committed(Set<TopicPartition> partitions)\n```\n\nMakes a remote call to the coordinator to fetch the last committed offsets for the given partitions. If a partition has no committed offset, its entry in the result map is `null`.\n\nBlocks until the offsets are fetched or `default.api.timeout.ms` expires (`TimeoutException`).\n\n#### `committed(Set<TopicPartition> partitions, Duration timeout)`\n\n```java\nMap<TopicPartition, OffsetAndMetadata> committed(Set<TopicPartition> partitions, Duration timeout)\n```\n\nSame with an explicit timeout.\n\n### 6.6 Current Position\n\n#### `position(TopicPartition partition)`\n\n```java\nlong position(TopicPartition partition)\n```\n\nReturns the offset of the *next* record that will be fetched. May issue a remote call if the position is not yet known (e.g., immediately after assignment, before the first `poll()`).\n\nBlocks until the position is determined or `default.api.timeout.ms` expires.\n\n**Throws:** `IllegalStateException` if the partition is not assigned. `InvalidOffsetException` if no offset is defined. `TimeoutException` if position cannot be resolved in time.\n\n#### `position(TopicPartition partition, Duration timeout)`\n\n```java\nlong position(TopicPartition partition, Duration timeout)\n```\n\nSame with an explicit timeout.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Flow Control and Position Queries\n\n### 7.1 Pause and Resume\n\n#### `pause(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions)`\n\n```java\nvoid pause(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions)\n```\n\nSuspends fetching for the given partitions. Future `poll()` calls will not return records from these partitions until `resume()` is called. The partition remains assigned; it is just not fetched.\n\n- Does **not** trigger a group rebalance.\n- **Paused state is NOT preserved across rebalances.** After a rebalance, all partitions resume fetching.\n- Useful for coordinating back-pressure in multi-threaded processing.\n\n**Throws:** `IllegalStateException` if any partition is not currently assigned.\n\n#### `resume(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions)`\n\n```java\nvoid resume(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions)\n```\n\nResumes fetching for the given partitions. If a partition was not paused, this is a no-op.\n\n**Throws:** `IllegalStateException` if any partition is not currently assigned.\n\n#### `paused()`\n\n```java\nSet<TopicPartition> paused()\n```\n\nReturns the set of currently paused partitions.\n\n### 7.2 Offset Discovery\n\n#### `offsetsForTimes(Map<TopicPartition, Long> timestampsToSearch)`\n\n```java\nMap<TopicPartition, OffsetAndTimestamp> offsetsForTimes(Map<TopicPartition, Long> timestampsToSearch)\n```\n\nFor each partition, finds the earliest offset whose record timestamp is **≥** the provided timestamp (milliseconds since epoch). The consumer **does not have to be assigned** those partitions.\n\n- Returns `null` for a partition if no record with a matching timestamp exists within the timeout.\n- Returns `null` for a partition if the message format is pre-0.10.0 (no timestamps).\n- Blocks until all offsets are found or `default.api.timeout.ms` expires.\n\n**Throws:** `IllegalArgumentException` if any target timestamp is negative. `UnsupportedVersionException` if broker version does not support timestamp-based lookup.\n\n#### `offsetsForTimes(Map<TopicPartition, Long> timestampsToSearch, Duration timeout)`\n\n```java\nMap<TopicPartition, OffsetAndTimestamp> offsetsForTimes(Map<TopicPartition, Long> timestampsToSearch, Duration timeout)\n```\n\nSame with an explicit timeout.\n\n#### `beginningOffsets(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions)`\n\n```java\nMap<TopicPartition, Long> beginningOffsets(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions)\n```\n\nReturns the log start offset (earliest available) for each partition. Does **not** change the consumer's current position.\n\n#### `beginningOffsets(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions, Duration timeout)`\n\n```java\nMap<TopicPartition, Long> beginningOffsets(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions, Duration timeout)\n```\n\nSame with an explicit timeout. Returns an empty map if the timeout is zero.\n\n#### `endOffsets(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions)`\n\n```java\nMap<TopicPartition, Long> endOffsets(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions)\n```\n\nReturns the end offset for each partition:\n- `read_uncommitted`: high watermark (last replicated message offset + 1)\n- `read_committed`: Last Stable Offset (LSO)\n- Unwritten partition: 0\n\nDoes **not** change the consumer's position.\n\n#### `endOffsets(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions, Duration timeout)`\n\n```java\nMap<TopicPartition, Long> endOffsets(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions, Duration timeout)\n```\n\nSame with an explicit timeout. Returns an empty map if the timeout is zero.\n\n#### `currentLag(TopicPartition topicPartition)`\n\n```java\nOptionalLong currentLag(TopicPartition topicPartition)\n```\n\nReturns the consumer's lag (end offset − position) for the given partition using **locally cached** metadata. Returns an empty `OptionalLong` if the position or end offset is not yet known. If the end offset is unknown, triggers a background fetch but returns immediately without blocking.\n\n**Throws:** `IllegalStateException` if the partition is not assigned.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Metadata and Monitoring\n\n### `partitionsFor(String topic)`\n\n```java\nList<PartitionInfo> partitionsFor(String topic)\n```\n\nFetches partition metadata for a topic from the broker. Returns an empty list if the topic does not exist. Blocks for up to `default.api.timeout.ms`.\n\n### `partitionsFor(String topic, Duration timeout)`\n\n```java\nList<PartitionInfo> partitionsFor(String topic, Duration timeout)\n```\n\nSame with an explicit timeout.\n\n### `listTopics()`\n\n```java\nMap<String, List<PartitionInfo>> listTopics()\n```\n\nReturns partition metadata for all topics the authenticated user is authorized to view. Issues a remote call to the broker.\n\n### `listTopics(Duration timeout)`\n\n```java\nMap<String, List<PartitionInfo>> listTopics(Duration timeout)\n```\n\nSame with an explicit timeout.\n\n### `metrics()`\n\n```java\nMap<MetricName, ? extends Metric> metrics()\n```\n\nReturns all metrics tracked by this consumer instance. Metrics include fetch rates, commit rates, rebalance counts, lag, and more.\n\n### `clientInstanceId(Duration timeout)`\n\n```java\nUuid clientInstanceId(Duration timeout)\n```\n\nReturns the unique client instance ID used for telemetry. Requires a cluster connection to generate (blocks up to `timeout`). Requires `enable.metrics.push=true`.\n\n**Throws:** `IllegalStateException` if telemetry is not enabled.\n\n### `groupMetadata()`\n\n```java\nConsumerGroupMetadata groupMetadata()\n```\n\nReturns the current group metadata: `group.id`, `generation.id`, `member.id`, and (if set) `group.instance.id`.\n\n**Throws:** `InvalidGroupIdException` if the consumer does not have a group.\n\n### `registerMetricForSubscription(KafkaMetric metric)`\n\n```java\nvoid registerMetricForSubscription(KafkaMetric metric)\n```\n\nRegisters an application metric for inclusion in OpenTelemetry telemetry sent to the broker. Metric must map to an OTLP `Sum` (Counter) or `Gauge` (UpDownCounter) data point. Re-registering an existing metric updates its entry.\n\n### `unregisterMetricFromSubscription(KafkaMetric metric)`\n\n```java\nvoid unregisterMetricFromSubscription(KafkaMetric metric)\n```\n\nRemoves a previously registered application metric. No-op if the metric was not registered.\n\n---\n\n## 9. Lifecycle and Resource Management\n\n### `close()`\n\n```java\nvoid close()\n```\n\nCloses the consumer using the default leave group behavior and waits up to 30 seconds for cleanup. If auto-commit is enabled, attempts to commit current offsets before closing.\n\n- Executes all shutdown steps even if individual steps fail; logs all errors; throws the first error encountered.\n- **`wakeup()` cannot interrupt `close()`.**\n\n**Throws:** `WakeupException`, `InterruptException`, `KafkaException` (including errors from rebalance or commit callbacks).\n\n### `close(CloseOptions option)`\n\n```java\nvoid close(CloseOptions option)\n```\n\nCloses the consumer with explicit control over timeout and group membership behavior via `CloseOptions`. `CloseOptions` allows specifying:\n- A timeout (defaults to 30 seconds if not specified)\n- A `GroupMembershipOperation` (e.g., whether to send a LeaveGroup request)\n\nThe actual broker operation time is bounded by `request.timeout.ms`. Callback execution time (commit callbacks, rebalance callbacks) does not count against the close timeout.\n\n### `close(Duration timeout)` *(Deprecated since 4.1)*\n\n```java\n@Deprecated(since = \"4.1\")\nvoid close(Duration timeout)\n```\n\nDeprecated. Use `close(CloseOptions)` instead. Closes with the default leave group behavior and a custom timeout.\n\n### `wakeup()`\n\n```java\nvoid wakeup()\n```\n\n**Thread-safe.** Interrupts any blocking operation on the consumer thread by causing it to throw `WakeupException`. If no operation is currently blocking, the next blocking call will throw `WakeupException` instead.\n\nUse this for clean shutdown from a separate thread (see [Section 1](#1-overview-and-threading-model)).\n\n### `enforceRebalance(String reason)`\n\n```java\nvoid enforceRebalance(String reason)\n```\n\nNon-blocking. Forces the consumer to rejoin the group on the next `poll()`, triggering a rebalance. If a rebalance is already in progress, this is a no-op. You must still call `poll()` to initiate the actual rebalance.\n\nUseful when external state (encoded in `ConsumerPartitionAssignor.Subscription` user data) changes without Kafka being aware.\n\n**Throws:** `IllegalStateException` if the consumer is not using group subscription.\n\n### `enforceRebalance()`\n\n```java\nvoid enforceRebalance()\n```\n\nSame as `enforceRebalance(null)`.\n\n---\n\n## 10. Exception Handling Guide\n\n### `CommitFailedException`\n\nThrown by `commitSync()` when the commit fails and cannot be retried. This is a **fatal commit error**.\n\n**Root cause:** A group rebalance completed before the commit could be applied. Some partitions may have been reassigned to another consumer, so retrying the commit would be unsafe.\n\n**Default message:**\n> \"Commit cannot be completed since the group has already rebalanced and assigned the partitions to another member. This means that the time between subsequent calls to poll() was longer than the configured max.poll.interval.ms...\"\n\n**Resolution:**\n1. Increase `max.poll.interval.ms` to give processing more time.\n2. Reduce `max.poll.records` to process fewer records per poll iteration.\n3. Move heavy processing to a worker thread pool (with `pause()`/`resume()` coordination).\n\n### `RetriableCommitFailedException`\n\nSubclass of `CommitFailedException` for retriable commit failures. Can be retried after a brief delay.\n\n### `WakeupException`\n\nThrown when `wakeup()` is called while a thread is blocked in `poll()`, `commitSync()`, `position()`, or other blocking operations. Not a fatal error — designed for clean shutdown signaling.\n\n```java\ntry {\n    while (running) {\n        records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofSeconds(1));\n        process(records);\n    }\n} catch (WakeupException e) {\n    if (running) throw e; // Unexpected — re-throw\n    // Expected shutdown — fall through to close()\n} finally {\n    consumer.close();\n}\n```\n\n### `RebalanceInProgressException`\n\nThrown by `commitSync()` when a rebalance is underway and the final assignment is not yet known. **Not fatal** — call `poll()` to complete the rebalance, then retry the commit (with updated offsets, since the assignment may have changed).\n\n### `NoOffsetForPartitionException`\n\nThrown when a partition has no committed offset and `auto.offset.reset=none`. Set `auto.offset.reset` to `earliest` or `latest`, or call `seek()` explicitly before polling.\n\n### `OffsetOutOfRangeException`\n\nThrown when the consumer's position falls outside the range `[logStartOffset, logEndOffset]` and `auto.offset.reset=none`.\n\n### `LogTruncationException`\n\nThrown when the broker reports that the log was truncated and the consumer's position is now invalid (e.g., after a leader election with unclean failover). Consumer should reset position.\n\n### `InvalidOffsetException`\n\nBase class for `NoOffsetForPartitionException` and `OffsetOutOfRangeException`.\n\n### `AuthenticationException`\n\nAuthentication with the broker failed. Fatal — check security configuration.\n\n### `AuthorizationException`\n\nConsumer lacks `Read` ACL on a topic, the `group.id`, or a transaction ID. Fatal for that topic/group.\n\n### `FencedInstanceIdException`\n\nThe consumer's `group.instance.id` (static membership) was fenced by the broker — another instance with the same ID joined the group. The fenced consumer should stop polling and close.\n\n### `InterruptException`\n\nWraps `InterruptedException` from thread interruption. Thread interrupt status is restored on throw. Prefer `wakeup()` over interrupts when possible.\n\n### `UnsupportedVersionException`\n\nThe broker does not support the requested feature (e.g., stable offsets with `read_committed`, RE2/J subscriptions). Upgrade the broker or disable the feature.\n\n### `TimeoutException`\n\nA blocking operation (commit, position lookup, metadata fetch) did not complete within the configured timeout. May be retriable depending on context.\n\n---\n\n## 11. Configuration-Driven Behaviors\n\nThe following configurations significantly affect API behavior:\n\n| Property | Default | Effect |\n|----------|---------|--------|\n| `bootstrap.servers` | *(required)* | Initial broker contact for cluster discovery |\n| `group.id` | `\"\"` | Consumer group identifier; required for group management |\n| `group.instance.id` | `null` | Static membership ID; prevents unnecessary rebalances on restart |\n| `group.protocol` | `CLASSIC` | `CLASSIC` or `CONSUMER`; the `CONSUMER` protocol is the newer rebalance protocol |\n| `enable.auto.commit` | `true` | Whether offsets are committed automatically |\n| `auto.commit.interval.ms` | `5000` | Frequency of automatic offset commits (only when `enable.auto.commit=true`) |\n| `auto.offset.reset` | `latest` | What to do when no committed offset exists: `earliest`, `latest`, or `none` |\n| `max.poll.records` | `500` | Maximum records returned per `poll()` call |\n| `max.poll.interval.ms` | `300000` | Max time between `poll()` calls before the consumer is evicted from the group |\n| `session.timeout.ms` | `45000` | Max time without a heartbeat before the broker considers the consumer dead |\n| `heartbeat.interval.ms` | `3000` | Frequency of heartbeats sent to the broker |\n| `fetch.min.bytes` | `1` | Minimum data the server should return per fetch; broker waits until this is satisfied |\n| `fetch.max.bytes` | `52428800` | Maximum data per fetch response (50 MB) |\n| `fetch.max.wait.ms` | `500` | Max time the broker waits to satisfy `fetch.min.bytes` |\n| `max.partition.fetch.bytes` | `1048576` | Maximum bytes per partition per fetch (1 MB) |\n| `isolation.level` | `read_uncommitted` | `read_uncommitted` or `read_committed`; affects which records are visible |\n| `default.api.timeout.ms` | `60000` | Default timeout for blocking API calls (`commitSync`, `position`, `committed`, etc.) |\n| `request.timeout.ms` | `30000` | Timeout for broker requests; bounds the effective wait in `close()` |\n| `metadata.max.age.ms` | `300000` | How often metadata is refreshed; affects how quickly pattern subscriptions pick up new topics |\n| `partition.assignment.strategy` | `RangeAssignor` | Class(es) implementing `ConsumerPartitionAssignor` |\n| `enable.metrics.push` | `true` | Whether to push metrics telemetry to the broker |\n\n---\n\n## 12. Common Patterns and Best Practices\n\n### 12.1 Basic Subscription and Polling Loop (Auto-Commit)\n\n```java\nProperties props = new Properties();\nprops.setProperty(\"bootstrap.servers\", \"localhost:9092\");\nprops.setProperty(\"group.id\", \"my-group\");\nprops.setProperty(\"enable.auto.commit\", \"true\");\nprops.setProperty(\"auto.commit.interval.ms\", \"1000\");\nprops.setProperty(\"key.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\nprops.setProperty(\"value.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\n\ntry (KafkaConsumer<String, String> consumer = new KafkaConsumer<>(props)) {\n    consumer.subscribe(Arrays.asList(\"orders\", \"payments\"));\n\n    while (true) {\n        ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n        for (ConsumerRecord<String, String> record : records) {\n            System.out.printf(\"topic=%s partition=%d offset=%d key=%s value=%s%n\",\n                record.topic(), record.partition(), record.offset(), record.key(), record.value());\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n> **Caution with auto-commit:** Records are considered consumed as soon as they are returned by `poll()`. If the process crashes after receiving records but before processing them, those records are lost (at-most-once semantics can result). Ensure all records from a poll batch are fully processed before the next `poll()` call, otherwise committed offsets may advance beyond processed positions.\n\n### 12.2 Manual Offset Commit (At-Least-Once)\n\n```java\nProperties props = new Properties();\nprops.setProperty(\"bootstrap.servers\", \"localhost:9092\");\nprops.setProperty(\"group.id\", \"my-group\");\nprops.setProperty(\"enable.auto.commit\", \"false\");\nprops.setProperty(\"key.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\nprops.setProperty(\"value.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\n\ntry (KafkaConsumer<String, String> consumer = new KafkaConsumer<>(props)) {\n    consumer.subscribe(Arrays.asList(\"orders\"));\n\n    final int minBatchSize = 200;\n    List<ConsumerRecord<String, String>> buffer = new ArrayList<>();\n\n    while (true) {\n        ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n        for (ConsumerRecord<String, String> record : records) {\n            buffer.add(record);\n        }\n        if (buffer.size() >= minBatchSize) {\n            insertIntoDatabase(buffer);\n            // Commit AFTER successful processing\n            consumer.commitSync();\n            buffer.clear();\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nFor per-partition commit using `nextOffsets()` (Kafka 4.0+):\n\n```java\nwhile (running) {\n    ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(Long.MAX_VALUE));\n\n    for (TopicPartition partition : records.partitions()) {\n        List<ConsumerRecord<String, String>> partitionRecords = records.records(partition);\n        processAll(partitionRecords);\n    }\n\n    // Commit all partitions using the pre-computed next offsets\n    consumer.commitSync(records.nextOffsets());\n}\n```\n\n### 12.3 Rebalance Listener with Manual Offset Management\n\n```java\npublic class SaveOffsetsOnRebalance implements ConsumerRebalanceListener {\n    private final KafkaConsumer<?, ?> consumer;\n    private final OffsetStore store; // your custom offset store\n\n    public SaveOffsetsOnRebalance(KafkaConsumer<?, ?> consumer, OffsetStore store) {\n        this.consumer = consumer;\n        this.store = store;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void onPartitionsRevoked(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\n        // Commit current positions to external store BEFORE giving up partitions\n        for (TopicPartition partition : partitions) {\n            store.saveOffset(partition, consumer.position(partition));\n        }\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void onPartitionsAssigned(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\n        // Restore positions from external store for newly assigned partitions\n        for (TopicPartition partition : partitions) {\n            Long savedOffset = store.getOffset(partition);\n            if (savedOffset != null) {\n                consumer.seek(partition, savedOffset);\n            } else {\n                consumer.seekToBeginning(Collections.singleton(partition));\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void onPartitionsLost(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\n        // Partitions were lost without a graceful revoke (e.g., session timeout)\n        // Do NOT commit offsets here — another consumer may already own these partitions\n        // Just clean up local state\n        for (TopicPartition partition : partitions) {\n            store.clearLocalState(partition);\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n// Usage:\nconsumer.subscribe(Arrays.asList(\"my-topic\"), new SaveOffsetsOnRebalance(consumer, offsetStore));\n```\n\n**Callback ordering guarantees:**\n- Under normal conditions: all `onPartitionsRevoked` callbacks fire across all group members **before** any `onPartitionsAssigned` callbacks fire.\n- Exception: session timeout causes a partition to be reassigned without the old owner's `onPartitionsRevoked` being invoked. The old owner later fires `onPartitionsLost` when it realizes it no longer owns those partitions.\n- Under the CONSUMER protocol (and CLASSIC with cooperative mode): `onPartitionsRevoked` fires only when partitions are actually revoked (non-empty). Under CLASSIC eager mode: `onPartitionsRevoked` fires with the full assignment (even if nothing changes).\n- `onPartitionsAssigned` fires even if no new partitions were assigned, enabling it as a \"rebalance complete\" notification.\n\n### 12.4 Seek Operations\n\n```java\n// Seek to the beginning of all assigned partitions\nconsumer.seekToBeginning(consumer.assignment());\n\n// Seek to the end of all assigned partitions\nconsumer.seekToEnd(consumer.assignment());\n\n// Seek to a specific offset\nconsumer.seek(new TopicPartition(\"orders\", 0), 1234L);\n\n// Seek to a point in time (replay from 1 hour ago)\nMap<TopicPartition, Long> timestamps = new HashMap<>();\nfor (TopicPartition tp : consumer.assignment()) {\n    timestamps.put(tp, System.currentTimeMillis() - Duration.ofHours(1).toMillis());\n}\n\nMap<TopicPartition, OffsetAndTimestamp> offsets = consumer.offsetsForTimes(timestamps);\nfor (Map.Entry<TopicPartition, OffsetAndTimestamp> entry : offsets.entrySet()) {\n    if (entry.getValue() != null) {\n        consumer.seek(entry.getKey(), entry.getValue().offset());\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Important seek notes:**\n- `seekToBeginning` and `seekToEnd` are **lazy**: the position is not resolved until the next `poll()` or `position()` call.\n- `seek(partition, offset)` is **immediate**: the internal position is updated synchronously.\n- Seeking to an offset outside `[logStartOffset, logEndOffset]` triggers `auto.offset.reset` behavior.\n- Seeking does not affect the committed offset in Kafka — only the in-memory fetch position.\n\n### 12.5 Multi-Threaded Processing with Pause/Resume\n\n```java\n// Single consumer thread dispatches to a worker pool.\n// Pause prevents the consumer from receiving new records while workers are busy.\n\nExecutorService executor = Executors.newFixedThreadPool(8);\nMap<TopicPartition, Future<?>> activeTasks = new HashMap<>();\n\nwhile (true) {\n    // Resume partitions whose workers have completed\n    activeTasks.entrySet().removeIf(entry -> {\n        if (entry.getValue().isDone()) {\n            consumer.resume(Collections.singleton(entry.getKey()));\n            return true;\n        }\n        return false;\n    });\n\n    ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n\n    for (TopicPartition partition : records.partitions()) {\n        List<ConsumerRecord<String, String>> partitionRecords = records.records(partition);\n        if (!activeTasks.containsKey(partition)) {\n            // Pause this partition to prevent more records arriving before the worker finishes\n            consumer.pause(Collections.singleton(partition));\n            Future<?> task = executor.submit(() -> {\n                processRecords(partitionRecords);\n                // Note: offset commit requires coordination with the consumer thread\n            });\n            activeTasks.put(partition, task);\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n> **Key constraint:** Offset commits must happen on the consumer thread. Worker threads signal completion; the consumer thread then commits and resumes. This design avoids race conditions between commit and partition reassignment.\n\n### 12.6 Async Commit with Sync Fallback on Shutdown\n\nA common pattern for high-throughput consumers: use non-blocking `commitAsync()` during normal operation and `commitSync()` only on shutdown to ensure the final offsets are committed.\n\n```java\ntry {\n    while (running) {\n        ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(100));\n        processRecords(records);\n\n        // Non-blocking; failed commits are logged but not retried\n        consumer.commitAsync((offsets, exception) -> {\n            if (exception != null) {\n                log.warn(\"Async commit failed for {}\", offsets, exception);\n            }\n        });\n    }\n} catch (CommitFailedException e) {\n    log.error(\"Commit failed, likely due to rebalance\", e);\n} finally {\n    try {\n        // Blocking commit on shutdown to ensure the last batch is committed\n        consumer.commitSync();\n    } finally {\n        consumer.close();\n    }\n}\n```\n\n### 12.7 Manual Partition Assignment (Standalone Consumer)\n\n```java\nString topic = \"audit-log\";\n// Fetch partition metadata to discover available partitions\nList<PartitionInfo> partitions = consumer.partitionsFor(topic);\n\nList<TopicPartition> topicPartitions = partitions.stream()\n    .map(p -> new TopicPartition(p.topic(), p.partition()))\n    .collect(Collectors.toList());\n\nconsumer.assign(topicPartitions);\n\n// Optionally seek to beginning for a full replay\nconsumer.seekToBeginning(topicPartitions);\n\nwhile (true) {\n    ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(1000));\n    for (ConsumerRecord<String, String> record : records) {\n        processRecord(record);\n    }\n    consumer.commitSync();\n}\n```\n\n**Differences from subscribed consumer:**\n- No rebalance, no heartbeat for group purposes, no `ConsumerRebalanceListener`.\n- Partition assignment does not change unless `assign()` is called again.\n- Consumer failures do not cause partition reassignment.\n- `group.id` can still be used for offset storage, but use a unique ID per consumer instance to avoid commit conflicts.\n\n### 12.8 Transactional Message Consumption\n\n```java\nProperties props = new Properties();\nprops.setProperty(\"bootstrap.servers\", \"localhost:9092\");\nprops.setProperty(\"group.id\", \"transactional-consumer\");\nprops.setProperty(\"isolation.level\", \"read_committed\"); // Only see committed transactions\nprops.setProperty(\"enable.auto.commit\", \"false\");\nprops.setProperty(\"key.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\nprops.setProperty(\"value.deserializer\", \"org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.StringDeserializer\");\n\ntry (KafkaConsumer<String, String> consumer = new KafkaConsumer<>(props)) {\n    consumer.subscribe(Arrays.asList(\"transactional-topic\"));\n\n    while (true) {\n        ConsumerRecords<String, String> records = consumer.poll(Duration.ofMillis(1000));\n        // Records from aborted transactions are automatically filtered out\n        // Offsets may appear non-consecutive due to filtered transaction markers and aborted records\n        for (ConsumerRecord<String, String> record : records) {\n            processRecord(record);\n        }\n        consumer.commitSync();\n    }\n}\n```\n\n**Transactional semantics notes:**\n- In `read_committed` mode, `poll()` returns only records from committed transactions plus all non-transactional records.\n- Records from aborted transactions are filtered out. Their offsets remain in the log, creating gaps in returned offsets.\n- Transaction markers (commit/abort) also occupy log offsets but are not returned to the application — another source of offset gaps.\n- `endOffsets()` and `seekToEnd()` return the LSO (not the HWM) for `read_committed` consumers.\n- Fetch lag metrics are reported relative to the LSO for `read_committed` consumers.\n\n---\n\n*This documentation reflects the Apache Kafka KafkaConsumer API as found in the `org.apache.kafka.clients.consumer` package. For full configuration reference, see [`ConsumerConfig`](https://kafka.apache.org/documentation/#consumerconfigs). Broker version compatibility: requires broker ≥ 0.10.0; individual features may require higher versions.*\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2687,"cache_read_input_tokens":57442,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":2687,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0},"output_tokens":8,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"aaf3bda1-23d5-4d94-ae86-e598b1b1f60f","uuid":"4787e539-0b10-40f8-8aaf-22d5812a9a06"}
